<div id="review_562703449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/562703449" />
    <a title="Christopher Herz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4183292-christopher-herz"><img alt="Christopher Herz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442515495p2/4183292.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/562703449?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christopher Herz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christopher Herz" href="/user/show/4183292-christopher-herz">Christopher Herz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer562703449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12328691749431714318">This is one of my top 5 novels of all time. For me, it has everything I need in a book. That quality that makes you put it down and say, or scream DAMN! HOW DID HE DO THAT?<br/><br/>Milan Kundera seems to transcend writing - I can't explain it or figure out how he did it, but the experience of reading this book made me shake and tremble and wonder if there was magic being spilled onto the pages. The story, characters and writing were all so amazing I feel that no other writer can come close to what he did</span>
  <span id="freeText12328691749431714318" style="display:none">This is one of my top 5 novels of all time. For me, it has everything I need in a book. That quality that makes you put it down and say, or scream DAMN! HOW DID HE DO THAT?<br /><br />Milan Kundera seems to transcend writing - I can't explain it or figure out how he did it, but the experience of reading this book made me shake and tremble and wonder if there was magic being spilled onto the pages. The story, characters and writing were all so amazing I feel that no other writer can come close to what he did.<br /><br />Though "The Book of Laughter and Forgetting" and "The Unbearable Lightness of Being" are thought to be his best, I believe this book is his masterpiece and for me at least, is held up as the work of fiction that we should all march towards in terms of quality of a novel.<br /><br />It is, to me, the very essence of a novel. Amazing. Please read and let me know what you think.<br /><br />-CH</span>

  <span id="freeText570335350019327323" style="display:none">For the majority of this book, I thought how Kundera was maybe not for me anymore, that I could still see how clever and sarcastic his work was but I just didn't feel like being thrown into the ugly pond of it all, so I wasn't going to play his game... but the last part with the inside Joke changed things and I can't help being impressed once again. Well done. <br /><br /><i>(A few days later)</i><br />But... I'm rating books mainly based on my enjoyment and it just wasn't there for the most part. I do think it is a very good book. It's definitely not for everyone; you could enjoy this if you enjoyed other Kundera's books or if you don't mind reading about insufferable characters, horribly toxic relationships and stuff like that. I guess I wasn't in the mood for this or these characters and their behavior were just too much for me to be able to enjoy the book.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13281276892598178282">Like falling from one dream into another this novel takes you on a journey into the adolescence of a poet. Peeling away layers of personality the poet protagonist is revealed to be a human with all the ridiculous accouterments that attend to the artist. Kundera at his best in the sense that he portrays life with a broad philosophic and humane touch. For those who enjoy ideas and feeling the sublime this is a great novel.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1386302570" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1386302570" />
    <a title="Amirtha Shri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29509433-amirtha-shri"><img alt="Amirtha Shri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586863457p2/29509433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1386302570?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amirtha Shri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amirtha Shri" href="/user/show/29509433-amirtha-shri">Amirtha Shri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1386302570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18099504100569177578">"Why was he so foolish as to want to step on to the throat of his own song? What was the sense of giving up poetry for the sake of revolution?"<br/><br/>Jaromil, a plunged product of mother's prodigious love, transforms from a pet to an artist to a poet to a communist, and somehow cannot be all of them at the same time which is possibly the bane of his existence. Each transfiguration subverts a part of his flatness and adds to him something unsavory. This book has so much substance scattered all over and </span>
  <span id="freeText18099504100569177578" style="display:none">"Why was he so foolish as to want to step on to the throat of his own song? What was the sense of giving up poetry for the sake of revolution?"<br /><br />Jaromil, a plunged product of mother's prodigious love, transforms from a pet to an artist to a poet to a communist, and somehow cannot be all of them at the same time which is possibly the bane of his existence. Each transfiguration subverts a part of his flatness and adds to him something unsavory. This book has so much substance scattered all over and it is safe to say that the plot is but a trifling scam.<br /><br />"You think that just because it's already happened, the past is finished and unchangeable? Oh no, the past is cloaked in multicolored taffeta and every time we look at it we see a different hue."<br /><br />Kundera explores what it is to love and be loved in the most unpalatable fashion, how it is to exude a plethora of untainted artistry and how it is to corrupt it with the course of life, and what a toll a communist revolution can take on a vainglorious artist's unsophisticated acumen.<br /><br />What I enjoyed the best in this story is the charm of the telling. Kundera has nonchalantly slobbered interludes of direct questions and comments. Similar to how Jaromil deprives humans their humanity in his art, Kundera does the same in his book by depriving people their names. This book is heavy with references to poets and their anecdotes and their parallels to Jaromil which makes it an absolute literary delight.<br /><br />"Then what distinguishes the tragic from the ridiculous? The mere accident of success? What distinguishes pettiness from greatness, anyway? Tell us, Lermontov!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="18099504100569177578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('steC4pBumUZsH9PpqH+qrjVkXQ7DVxuFuQOsVLUjcLMByfQVNpGLSzUb9tq0QsXjzGZdU8IhNYHQrOZBvnsoVQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5TRt3Cc7DUtPlBUbUjkqrOEAWK+mN6COEoaavwfLt+NWKhsrgcQfRhaQMChOBEXhGAJY8qdBjop7KdCqDJPvBQ==')})
  }

Επίσης είναι ένα μυθιστόρημα για τα τρομερά γεγονότα που συγκλόνισαν τον κόσμο, και για άλλα, λιγότερο τρομερά, που τον συγκλόνισαν επίσης. \n\nΗ ιστορία αρχίζει <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2137398678867532643\" style=\"display:none\">Το Eργοστάσιο των μολυβιών είναι ένα μυθιστόρημα για την επανάσταση και τους επαναστάτες. Επίσης είναι ένα μυθιστόρημα για τα τρομερά γεγονότα που συγκλόνισαν τον κόσμο, και για άλλα, λιγότερο τρομερά, που τον συγκλόνισαν επίσης. \n\nΗ ιστορία αρχίζει το 1866, στο Κάιρο, όταν χτίζεται η διώρυγα του Σουέζ, και τελειώνει στην Αθήνα λίγες μέρες πριν από τον B\' Παγκόσμιο Πόλεμο. Πρόκειται για το χρονικό μιας ελληνικής αστικής οικογένειας που δεν μοιάζει με τις άλλες, και που δεν συμμορφώνεται με την ηθική του δέκατου ένατου αιώνα. \nΑκόμα, πρόκειται για την ιστορία μιας μεγάλης φιλίας, που αρχίζει στη Ζυρίχη και που συνεχίζεται στις ταραγμένες πόλεις του κόσμου: στο Βερολίνο και στην Αγία Πετρούπολη. \n\nΣτο Εργοστάσιο των μολυβιών οι ήρωες βρίσκονται στη δίνη των πολιτικών γεγονότων, από τις αιματηρές εξεγέρσεις κατά της αποικιοκρατικής εξουσίας μέχρι την Οκτωβριανή Επανάσταση, κι από την παραφορά της μετεπαναστατικής Ρωσίας μέχρι τα εγκλήματα του σταλινικού καθεστώτος κι ανάμεσα σ\' αυτά τα γεγονότα συμβαίνουν άλλα, όχι λιγότερο συνταρακτικά: ο έρωτας, η απελπισία, η αρρώστια, και τα παιχνίδια της τύχης. \n\nΤο Eργοστάσιο των μολυβιών είναι ένα βιβλίο για τον άνθρωπο-τεχνικό και για τον άνθρωπο επαναστάτη, που είναι συχνά το ίδιο. Právě jeho „českému život<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17920577795726588602\" style=\"display:none\">Jan Novák, proslulý dosud svými povídkovými a románovými opusy, předstupuje nyní před čtenáře s žánrem literární biografie. Centrem jeho pozornosti je Milan Kundera, ve světě dnes asi nejznámější spisovatel s českými kořeny. Právě jeho „českému životu“ je věnován obsáhlý Novákův životopis, mapující ve čtyřech oddílech Kunderovo rodinné zázemí, autorovy básnické počátky ve znamení stalinismu padesátých let, prominentní působení v letech šedesátých a život v hledáčku Státní bezpečnosti před odchodem do exilu v první polovině sedmdesátých let, kdy Kundera už nesměl publikovat a na veřejnosti vystupoval mystifikačně pod pseudonymy.\nNovák nepíše standardní vědeckou biografii, ale životopis přiznaně osobní, v jehož šťavnaté hovorové češtině lze bezpečně rozpoznat autora románů o Mašínech (Zatím dobrý) nebo povídek o Češích v Americe (Hic a kosa v Chicagu). Vychází ovšem z pečlivého studia archivních pramenů, dobových dokumentů, osobních svědectví a Kunderových publikovaných textů, které na stránkách jeho knihy ožívají ve výmluvných citacích stejně jako <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5687692366640400332">Milan Kundera is a Czech and French writer of Czech origin who has lived in exile in France since 1975, where he became a naturalized French citizen in 1981. He is best known for <i>The Unbearable Lightness of Being</i>, <i>The Book of Laughter and Forgetting</i>, and <i>The Joke</i>.<br/><br/>Kundera has written in both Czech and French. He revises the French translations of all his books; these therefore are not considered tr</span>
  <span id="freeText5687692366640400332" style="display:none">Milan Kundera is a Czech and French writer of Czech origin who has lived in exile in France since 1975, where he became a naturalized French citizen in 1981. He is best known for <i>The Unbearable Lightness of Being</i>, <i>The Book of Laughter and Forgetting</i>, and <i>The Joke</i>.<br /><br />Kundera has written in both Czech and French. He revises the French translations of all his books; these therefore are not considered translations but original works. <br /><br />Due to censorship by the Communist government of Czechoslovakia, his books were banned from his native country, and that remained the case until the downfall of this government in the Velvet Revolution of 1989. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5687692366640400332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
